## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: solid mechanics / materials science (thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling)
**Analysis**: The variables are stress (sigma), strain (epsilon), and temperature (T), which is the standard setting for constitutive (stress–strain) laws including elastic, plastic, and thermal-softening effects. Typical relationships include linear/nonlinear elasticity in epsilon and temperature-dependent moduli or yield/flow stresses that decrease with increasing T.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke's law (isothermal linear elasticity): sigma = c0 * epsilon (small-strain elastic response)
- Thermoelastic modulus (linear in T): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (temperature-dependent Young's modulus)
- Exponential modulus softening: sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * T) * epsilon (rapid stiffening/softening with temperature)
- Nonlinear (cubic) elasticity: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**3 (rubber-like or higher-order elastic nonlinearity)
- Elastic + offset (residual/pre-stress): sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon (pre-stress plus linear elasticity)
- Power-law (Hollomon-type) hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (post-yield strain hardening when elastic strain is neglected/absorbed)
- Ramberg–Osgood-style inversion surrogate: sigma = c0 * epsilon / (c1 + epsilon**c2) (smooth transition from linear to nonlinear compliance behavior)
- Saturating stress with strain: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) (approach to a limiting stress with increasing strain)
- Temperature-softened hardening (separable): sigma = (c0 * exp(c1 * T)) * epsilon**c2 (hardening modulated by thermal softening/stiffening)
- Johnson–Cook-like thermal softening factor (simplified): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 - (c3 * T)**c4) (plastic flow stress reduced by temperature)
- Thermal activation-like softening without 1/T: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) / (1 + exp(c3 + c4 * T)) (sigmoidal drop of strength with T across a transition)
- Coupled polynomial surface (empirical constitutive fit): sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon + c2 * T + c3 * epsilon * T + c4 * epsilon**2 (common regression form for thermo-mechanical datasets)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Elastic regime identification: sigma proportional to epsilon (possibly with slope varying with T) suggests a modulus E(T) multiplying epsilon.
- Thermal softening: monotone decrease of sigma with increasing T at fixed epsilon is often captured by factors like exp(c*T), 1/(1+exp(c*T)), or (1-(c*T)^m).
- Strain hardening: increasing curvature in sigma vs epsilon is commonly modeled by epsilon**n or by adding higher-order terms (epsilon**2, epsilon**3).
- Saturation/approach to a limit with strain: if sigma tends to a plateau as epsilon grows, use 1-exp(c*epsilon) or rational transition forms in epsilon.
- Thermo-mechanical coupling beyond separability: if the effect of T changes with strain level, include interaction terms like epsilon*T, epsilon**p * exp(c*T), or (c0+c1*T)*epsilon**n.
- Presence of pre-stress/residual stress: nonzero sigma at epsilon=0 is represented by an additive constant c0, potentially also T-dependent (c0+c1*T).
- Regime change with temperature (e.g., brittle-to-ductile transition): sharp changes in sigma vs T are well represented by logistic-like factors in T multiplying a strain-dependent backbone.
- Data with near-linear behavior at small strain and nonlinear at larger strain: use additive decomposition sigma = E(T)*epsilon + K(T)*epsilon**n to capture both regimes smoothly.
